Agni
Bharadv─Бja B─Бrhaspatya
48 verses: g─Бyatr─л, except vardham─Бn─Б 1, 6, anuс╣гс╣нubh 27, 47тАУ48, triс╣гс╣нubh 46, arranged in trcas ╠е
This lengthy hymn must, like the last one (VI.15), be dissolved into tr╠еcas in order to fit the numerical arrangement of the maс╣Зс╕Нala. As Proferes (2007: 9) points out, this is an assemblage of Bharadv─Бja kindling verses, similar to the collections made by the Vai┼Ыv─Бmitras (III.27) and the Atris (V.28), likewise placed at or near the end of their Agni cycle. Again, the content stays primarily focused on the ritual aspects of Agni. Personal and family names are found fairly commonly (see especially the second [vss. 4тАУ6, and cf. vs. 19] and fifth [vss. 13тАУ15] tr╠еcas). There are overt signs of unity within some of the tr╠еcas: for instance, both the second (vss. 4тАУ6) and the third tr╠еcas (vss. 7тАУ9) begin each verse with a form of тАЬyouтАЭ; a variant of this is found in the fifth tr╠еca (vss. 13тАУ15).

+Jamison Brereton Notes

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYou, Agni, have been appointed by the gods, the ministrant fo men, the descendants of manu, at all sacrifices.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

You, Agni, were established as Hotar of all sacrifices
by the gods for the human race.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The tr. тАЬfor the human raceтАЭ reads like a dative, but m─Б╠Бnuс╣гe j├бne is of course a locative. Unfortunately English lacks the тАЬbeiтАЭ / тАЬchezтАЭ locution that would idiomatically tr. this loc. ### 02-03 The first p─Бdas of these vss. end respectively in adhvar├й# and ├бdhvanaс╕е#, which seems to signal an awareness of the deeper etym. relationship between the two stems.

+Griffith

PRIEST of all sacrifices hast thou been appointed by the Gods,
Agni, amid the race of man.

+Geldner

Du, Agni, bist zum Priester aller Opfer von den G├╢ttern bei dem Menschenvolk bestellt.

+Grassmann

Zum Priester aller Opfer bist du von den G├╢ttern eingesetzt, O Agni f├╝r der Menschen Stamm.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAgni, doere of great deeds, creator, you know (how to travel over) with speed (great) roads and (little) paths at sacrifices.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Adhvanaс╕е patha┼Ыca = mah─Бm─Бrg─Бn, great roads; kс╣гudra m─Бrg─Бm┼Ыca, little roads or paths; i.e. put the sacrificer into the right way when he is going wrong in the ceremonial or sacrifice

+Jamison Brereton

For you, o ritual adept, know the ways and the paths in their straight course,
o strong-willed god Agni, very effective at the sacrifices.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Klein (DGRV II.122) tr. b path├б┼Ы ca dev─Б╠Б ├▒jas─Б as тАЬand the paths going straight unto the heavenly ones,тАЭ apparently reading dev─Б╠Б ├▒jas─Б as a cmpd., contrary to the Pp.

and all standard tr. (incl. mine), which separate deva as a voc. Although I think the voc. interpretation is correct, cf. X.73.7 path├│ devatr─Б╠Б├▒jaseva y─Б╠Бn─Бn тАЬтАж the paths as if going straight to the gods,тАЭ with the adv. devatr─Б╠Бimmed. preceding and construed with ├б├▒jas─Б. On the basis of X.73.7 and similar phraseology, Insler (KZ 82 [1968] тАЬVedic ├б├▒jas─Б, с╣Ы├▒jas─Бn├б-, and the Type sahas─Бn├б-,тАЭ p. 6) takes dev─Б╠Б ├▒jas─Б as a shortening of devatr─Б╠Б ├▒jas─Б or тАЬa type of haplological abbreviation of devay─Б╠Б n─Бn ├б├▒jas─БтАЭ or possibly even directly as an тАЬadverbial-type compoundтАЭ dev─Б├▒j├бs─Б, and Klein must be flg. the Insler interpr. one way or the other. Although X.73.7 is suggestive, I do not think it is sufficient to allow the rather extreme type of haplology posited by Insler.

+Griffith

For well, O God, Disposer, thou knowest, straight on, the paths and ways,
Agni, most wise in sacrifice.

+Geldner

Denn du Meister kennst genau die Stra├Яen und Wege bei den Opfern, du wohlverst├дndiger Agni.

+Grassmann

Denn du, o Ordner, kennst, o Gott, die Wege und die Pfade stracks, Beim Opfer, Agni, einsichtsvoll.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬBharata, with the presenters of the oblation, has joyfully praised you in your (two-fold capacity), and has worshipped you, the adorable, with sacrifices.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Bharata: the r─Бj─Б, the son of Duс╣гyanta; in your two-fold capacity: in the character of bestowing what is wished for and removing wht is undesired; iс╣гс╣нa pr─Бptyaniс╣гс╣нa parih─Бrar┼лpeс╣З─Бgnir dvidh─Б

+Jamison Brereton

You does Bharata, along with his prizewinners, reverently invoke, now yet again, for blessing.
He has sacrificed to the sacrificial one at the sacrifices.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Klein (DGRV II.122) ascribes тАЬlogical conjunctive value тАШthereforeтАЩтАЭ to ├бdha here, connecting vss. 3 and 4. But since vs. 4 begins a new tс╣Ыca, it seems unlikely that vs. 4 is being conjoined to the tс╣Ыca-final vs. 3. Moreover, ├бdha here is displaced from its usual p─Бda-initial position to immediately precede dvit─Б╠Б, as it does several times elsewhere (I.132.3, VIII.1.28, 84.2, all p─Бda-final as here; also p─Бda-initial VIII.13.24 = IX.102.1, VIII.83.8). On the preceding page (DGRV II.121) Klein calls ├бdha dvit─Б╠Бa collocation and gives it тАЬquasi-formulaic status.тАЭ The occurrence here must belong to this group.

In b bharat├│ v─Бj├нbhiс╕е тАЬBharata with his prize-winnerтАЭ is an untranslatable pun on the poetтАЩs name Bharad-v─Бja, whose name appears in the next vs. (5c).

The ritualistic verbs ─лс╕╖e тАШreverently invokeтАЩ (a) and ─лj├й тАШsacrificeтАЩ (c) are exact rhymes (save for accent). I take them here as 3rd sg. , as do Geldner and Renou Although the 3rd sg. to the former stem is usually ─лс╣нс╣н╠Б e with ─лс╕╖ ╠Б e the 1st sg., in this context a 3rd sg. reading is favored, and the lack of accent on ─лс╕╖e allows it to be drawn into the morphological orbit of the pf. ─лj├й (cf. 3rd sg. perfect-accented ─лс╕Н├й in IV.3.3). K├╝mmel (389), flg. Tichy, takes both verbs as 1st sg., which is equally possible, as long as Bharata is referring to himself by name: тАЬYou do I, Bharata, reverently invoke тАжтАЭ

+Griffith

Thee, too, hath Bharata of old, with mighty men, implored for bliss.
And worshipped thee the worshipful.

+Geldner

Dich ruft nun abermals Bharata mit seinen Siegern erfolgreich an. Er hat bei den Opfern dem opferw├╝rdigen Agni geopfert.

+Grassmann

Dich pries zum Heil einst Bharata und mit den reichen opferte Bei Opfern er, dem Opferherrn.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬI glorify your splendour and the acts of you the liberal giver all who, (through your favour) enjoy their desires, glorify you.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Begin the sacrifice: your manifestation and your resolve do those of good drops,
the desirous ones, all take pleasure in.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

(pr├б) yakс╣гi is morphologically ambiguous – 2nd sg. act. -si impv. or 1st sg.

middle s-aor. – and opinion is divided: Oldenberg (ZDMG 55.314, Noten) dithers and doesnтАЩt ultimately decide; Geldner, Narten (Sig.Aor. 200-201), and Klein (DGRV I.385) opt for the 1st sg., Renou for the 2nd but to the root тИЪyakс╣г. A strong factor in favor of a 2nd sg. to тИЪyaj is the presence of an undoubted form of this same -si impv. in the following vs. (9c; cf. also 2c); in favor of a non-2nd-sg. interpr. is the difficulty of construing p─Бda-initial t├бva with such an impv. I consider the form the 2nd sg. act. to тИЪyaj, on the basis not only of 9c but also vs. 13 in the previous hymn (VI.15), where Agni is the subj. of a (pres.) impv. to pr├б тИЪyaj: VI.15.13d y├бjiс╣гс╣нс╕еaс╕е s├б pr├б yajat─Бm с╣Ыt─Б╠Бv─Б тАЬlet him, the best sacrificer, the truthful one, set the sacrifice in motion.тАЭ What then to do with the rest of the first two p─Бdas? I accept LudwigтАЩs suggestion (registered by Oldenberg) that pr├б yakс╣гi is a parenthesis – or rather, I think that, because of the rigid parallel patterning in this tс╣Ыca, t├бva, which belongs with the clause beginning saс╣Гdс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыam, has been fronted around the peremptory impv. pr├б yakс╣гi, and that it is dependent on the NP saс╣Гdс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыam ut├б kr├бtum: тАЬyour manifestation and resolve do they take pleasure in.тАЭ This is, strictly speaking, ungrammatical, but rhetoric occasionally trumps syntax.

+Griffith

I glorify thine aspect and the might of thee the Bountilul.
All those who love shall joy in thee,

+Geldner

Ich verehre deinen Anblick, und deinem Sinn willfahren die Freigebigen, alle, die einen Wunsch haben.

+Grassmann

Ich ehre deinen Anblick hoch, und schmecken sollen deine Kraft Die gabenreichen, heischenden.

+Elizarenkova

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Both Geldner and Renou supply тАШgodsтАЩ as the underlying object of v─лt├бye, and this is supported by dev├бv─лtaye in vs. 7 (and 41). But as in the previous hymn (VI.15.1, 14), I think the default object of тИЪv─л here is havy├б-, suggested by the name V─лta-havya, the poet to whom VI.15 is ascribed. Here the havy├б- can easily be extracted from the parallel purpose dative havy├б-d─Бtaye in b and its absence explained as gapping.

However, the Geldner/Renou solution is certainly possible, and there are no major implications either way.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe sage, Atharvan, extracted you from upon the lotus-leaf, the head, the support of the universe.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Tvam puс╣гkar─Бd adhi atharvo nirmanthata, murdhno viс╣гvasya v─Бghataс╕е: puс╣гkar─Бdadhi = puс╣гkaraparс╣Зe, lotus-leaf; puс╣гkara parс╣Зe praj─Бpatir bh┼лmim aparthayat = upon the lotus-leaf praj─Бpati made manifest the earth, a probable acount of the creation in Manu; since it supported the earth, it may be termed the head, m┼лrdhan, or the bearer, v─Бghata for v─Бhaka, of all things; atharvan means pr─Бс╣Зa, vital air extracted fire or animal heat from the water, pr─Бс╣Зa udakasak─Б┼Ы─Бd Agnim ni┼Ыeс╣гaс╣Зa mathitav─Бn;

V─Бghata = с╣Ыtvij, the ministrant priest; so the sentence is explained: all the priests churned you out of the head or top of the wood of attrition

+Jamison Brereton

You, Agni, did Atharvan churn forth from the lotus,
(did) the liturgists (churn) from the head of the whole (world?).

+Jamison Brereton Notes

On the ritual use of the lotus and the relevance of this vs., see Krick (Feuergr├╝ndung, 155-59), where (155) she calls this vs. тАЬdie Prim├дrquelle f├╝r die Verwendung eines Lotusblattes im Feuerritual.тАЭ In c v─Бgh├бtaс╕е can be gen. sg. or nom. pl. (as I take it, with Geldner and Renou). Since I donтАЩt know whatтАЩs going on here, I would certainly not exclude the gen. sg.: тАЬтАж (churned) from the head of every v─Бgh├бtтАЭ (so Krick 297) It is perhaps relevant that v├н┼Ыvasya v─Бgh├бtaс╕е phonologically echoes v├н┼Ыvasya j├бgataс╕е тАЬof the whole worldтАЭ (I.101.5, IV.13.3, VI.50.7, VII.60.2, 101.2, X.73.8).

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬCome, Agni, that I may address to you other praises in this manner; augment with these libations.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Other praises in this maner: ittthetar─Б giraс╕е = ittha, anena prak─Бreс╣Зa, thus, in this manner; also, offered by others, or by the asuras, asuraiс╕е kс╣Ыt─Б; Aitareya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa 3.49 cites this с╣Ыca: other than those offered to the gods, or adverse to the gods, propitiatory of the asuras, asurebhyaс╕е hitaс╕е devav─Бky─Бditara devavirodhinya ityarthaс╕е

+Jamison Brereton

Come here. I will speak to you, Agni, in this way: тАЬ(There are) other hymns,
but with these drops here you will become strong.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The stem ├нtara- is very rare in the RV and has a late distribution: besides this passage it is found only in the funeral hymns X.16.9-10 and X.18.1. This comparative isolation makes it difficult to determine its nuance here. Both Geldner and Renou (cf. also Klein DGRV I.266, Oberlies RdR I.242) think the phrase тАЬother hymnsтАЭ (├нtar─Б g├нraс╕е) refers to the hymns of a rival sacrificer (or sacrificers), and certainly the

-tara- suffix implies a choice of two, which has the further potential implication that one of them is bad. But, though the published translation rather vaguely reflects this interpr., I now think it is likely wrong. Instead, I think that the implicit contrast is between itth─Б╠Б тАШin just this wayтАЩ and ├нtara-, and I further think that ├нtar─Б g├нraс╕е is the acc. obj. of br├бv─Бс╣Зi, not the nom. subj. of a nominal clause in embedded direct speech. By this interpr. the speaker is telling Agni that in addition to the hymn or hymns he [=Agni] has already heard, the speaker will tell him other hymns in the same manner as the previous ones. In other words, he is promising a continuation of the recitation that has already pleased Agni, as well as promising to strengthen him with a physical offering тАФ the usual pairing of verbal and physical in the sacrifice. This interpr. follows that of Hertha Krick (Feuergr├╝ndung, p. 571): тАЬKomm herbei, Agni, sch├╢n will ich dir auf solche Weise noch andere Lobpreisungen sagen! Durch diese Tropfen sollst du wachsen.тАЭ I would now emend the tr. to тАЬCome here. I will speak other hymns to you, Agni, in this same way, and with these drops here you will become strong.тАЭ Oberlies claims that this is one of the only places in the RV that soma is pressed for Agni, but I do not see why the drops (├нndu-) canтАЩt be drops of ghee. To be sure, ├нndu- overwhelmingly refers to soma drops, but I donтАЩt think that soma has to be the referent.

+Griffith

Come, here, O Agni, will I sing verily other songs to thee,
And with these drops shalt thou grow strong.

+Geldner

Komm fein her, ich will es dir sagen: O Agni, die anderen Lobreden sind nur so. Du sollst dich an diesen Somas├дften st├дrken.

+Grassmann

Komm her, nun will ich singen gern noch andre Lieder, Agni, dir; Erquick an diesen Tr├дnken dich.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWheresoever, and upon whatsoever your mind is directed, you bestow uncommon vigour, and there you make your abode.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Wherever your mind is (set), (there) you will set your skill next, there you will make your seat.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the phonological resonance between 16b ├нtar─Бс╕е and 17b ├║ttaram.

The temptation is very strong to take dadhase, despite its lack of accent, as the verb of the subord. cl. introduced by y├бtra kv├а ca in p─Бda a, whose correlate t├бtra begins the last p─Бda (c). And indeed almost all interpr. (Oldenberg, Geldner, Renou, Klein DGRV I.266) have succumbed to this temptation. Oldenberg (ZDMG 55. 314-15) constructs an elaborate justification for the interpr., which he maintains in the Noten (though without the extensive special pleading). But despite OldenbergтАЩs claim (Noten) that тАЬdadhase kann nicht ohne Gezwungenheit als Hautptsatzverb aufgefasste werden,тАЭ I see no problem. I agree that a form of тИЪdh─Б should be supplied in the y├бtra clause – perhaps hit├бm, as in I.187.6 tv├й тАж m├бno hit├бm. The main clause of b, with its shortvowel subjunctive dadhase, expresses the next step in the process: after he has set his mind on something, he then will apply his skill to it – the progression from mental conception to physical realization that we frequently encounter in the RV. I take ├║ttara- here not as a qualification of value, тАШhigherтАЩ (e.g., KleinтАЩs тАЬhigher skillтАЭ), but as a temporal or logical тАШnext, laterтАЩ expressing the progress from a to b. The t├бtra clause of c gives us a third step, but the fact that this adverb correlates with y├бtra does not mean that the intermediate clause has to be under the domain of y├бtra.

There wilt thou gain a dwelling-place.

+Geldner

+Grassmann

Wo irgend sich dein Geist erregt, gewinnst du h├╢h’re Geisteskraft; Da schaffe du dir deinen Sitz.

+Elizarenkova

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Distressing to the eye: nahi p┼лrtam akс╣гipadbhuvat = akс╣гipat akс╣гс╣Зo pat─Бkam vin─Б┼Ыakam, the offender or destroyer of the eye

+Jamison Brereton

Since what is granted to you will not be (just) a speck, you good one, who are on (our) side,
therefore you will win (us) friendship.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

It is not clear whether te p┼лrt├бm refers to a gift given to Agni or by him.

The published translation takes it in the former sense, assuming that our gift to Agni will trigger his own actions for us in p─Бda c, in the standard reciprocal model of Vedic sacrifice.

Scarlatta (293), in keeping with his interpr. of nem─Бn─Бm (see below), also thinks itтАЩs a gift to Agni, but from others (тАЬwas [dir von anderen] geschenkt wirdтАЭ). Renou (see esp. his n.

expanding his tr.) takes it as AgniтАЩs gift to us, and I interpr. GeldnerтАЩs тАЬdeine SchenkungтАЭ in the same fashion. In fact, either interpr. is possible, and the choice will be influenced by oneтАЩs interpr. of p─Бda c.

The stem n├йma-, cognate to Aves. na─Уma- тАШhalfтАЩ, is implicitly oppositional, picking out one moiety or side, or simply тАЬsomeтАЭ out of a larger group. Here the unaccented gen. pl. nem─Бn─Бm, part of the voc. phrase headed by vaso, refers, in my view, to our side. This is clearly GeldnerтАЩs view because he footnotes his slightly awk.

тАЬdu Gott der einen ParteiтАЭ with тАЬDer Fromme oder Arier.тАЭ Other renderings are so awkward as to be almost unintelligible: Renou тАЬo Vasu, (dieu) de quelques-uns,тАЭ Klein (DGRV II.71) тАЬo Vasu of some (races).тАЭ And Scarlatta (293) takes it as referring to the opposition (тАЬo du Vasu der andereтАЭ), which then requires Agni to do some amends- making in p─Бda c. I consider it extremely unlikely that the poet would address Agni, the focus of his praise, as a god of just some people, diluting his power and denying his omnipresence – much less as a god of others. I might, however, slightly modify the published translation from тАЬon (our) sideтАЭ to тАЬof (our) side.тАЭ At first glance p─Бda c, ├бtho d├║vo vanavase, with its middle voice seems to involve AgniтАЩs winning d├║vas- for himself. This would be compatible with the Geldner/Renou interpr. of p─Бda a: if Agni gives us a not insignificant gift in p─Бda a, he has a good chance of winning our d├║vas- in c. However, the almost identical expression in the immediately preceding hymn, VI.15.6d dev├│ dev├йс╣гu v├бnate h├н no d├║vaс╕е тАЬfor the god will win friendship for us among the gods,тАЭ with the crucial loc. dev├йс╣гu and dat. of benefit naс╕е, suggests that Agni is winning something on our behalf. Cf. also, in this hymn, VI.16.28 agn├нr no vanate ray├нm тАЬAgni will win us wealth.тАЭ The root тИЪvan тАШwinтАЩ is strongly represented in this hymn, esp. in the middle section. Here we have vanavase; elsewhere vanv├бnn ├бv─Бtaс╕е 20, vanv├бn 26, vanv├бntaс╕е 27, vanate 28, as well as viv─Бsasi 12. This repetition cuts across tс╣Ыca boundaries.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬSurpassing all earthly things, may he bestow upon us riches, destroying his enemies by his greatness, unresisted, unassailed.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

For he will piously offer wealth beyond all earthly (goods) by his greatness,
winning (though) himself unwon, indestructible.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The root тИЪd─Б┼Ы тАШpiously serveтАЩ almost never takes an acc. object of the service or offering (but see vs. 31 below); moreover, it almost exclusively has a mortal subject and a god as recipient of the piety. Here, however, we have the opposite situation: it is impossible to avoid taking Agni as subject and a very concrete ray├нm as acc. object, with the implied recipients being us mortals. The clue here may be the preverb, as ├бti тИЪd─Б┼Ы in its other occurrence seems to mean something like тАШout-pious the piousтАЩ: magha├нr magh├│no ├бti ┼Ы┼лra d─Б┼Ыasi тАЬWith your bounties you outdo the bounteous ones in piety, o champion [=Indra].тАЭ Although the case frame is not exactly the same, the nuance is similar: human patrons are bounteous, but Indra is super-bounteous. In our passage Agni provides wealth тАЬbeyond all earthly (goods).тАЭ I previously thought that тАЬearthly goodsтАЭ were simply those material things that have their origins on/in the earth rather than heaven, but it may well be more pointed than that here: тАЬgoods that are given by those who stem from/dwell on earth, that is, humans.тАЭ So Agni outdoes human givers by providing wealth in excess of all the goods they can supply. On тАШgoodsтАЩ as the appropriate noun to supply with v├н┼Ыv─Б тАж p─Б╠Бrthiv─Б, cf. VI.45.20ab s├б h├н v├н┼Ыv─Бni p─Б╠Б rthiv─Бm╠Р, ├йko v├бs┼лni p├бtyate as well as VI.59.9, IX.100.3, X.111.10.

+Griffith

+Geldner

Denn er schenkt Reichtum ├╝ber alle irdischen Sch├дtze hinaus an Gr├╢├Яe, der unbesiegte, nie zu Fall gebrachte Sieger.

+Grassmann

Denn Gut gab er, das gr├╢sser ist als aller irdische Besitz, In Ruhe spendend, unverwehrt.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬSing praise and offer sacrifice, my friends, to the foe-discomfiting, the creator, Agni.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Comrades, boldly chant forth to Agni your praise and sacrifice and sing to the ritual adept.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda a contains a 2nd plural enclitic prn. and a plural voc. (vaс╕е sakh─Бyaс╕е тАЬto/of you, o comradesтАЭ), while c has two 2nd singular imperatives (├бrca g─Б╠Бya). The discrepancy in number must reflect the common situation of a poetтАЩs mixing address limited to himself with address to his colleagues and fellow ritual participants. So Geldner (n. 22), and see my 2009 тАЬPoetic Self-Reference in the Rig Veda and the Persona of Zarathustra,тАЭ BAI 19 (Fs. Skjaerv├╕). Geldner suggests without much enthusiasm that ├бrca g─Б╠Бya could be shortened 1st sg. subjunctives (*├бrc─Б *g─Б╠Бy─Б), evidently responding to Caland/HenryтАЩs reading the verbs thus in their 1906 LтАЩAgniс╣гс╣нoma, p. 428 (see Oldenberg, who likewise rejects it). ItтАЩs worth noting that VI.45.4 has the same configuration but with 2nd plural imperatives: s├бkh─Бyaс╕е тАж, ├бrcata pr├б ca g─Бyata тАЬo comrades, chant and sing forth тАжтАЭ This parallel is adduced by Bloomfield (Rig-Veda Repetitions) ad V.52.4, where he calls our verse тАЬa scrappy stanza тАжmodelled after existing patternsтАЭ (that is, VI.45.4). The parallel is certain apposite, but I doubt that our number discrepancy is simply the result of our poet jumbling together scraps drawn from different sources.

+Griffith

Give the Disposer praise and song.

+Geldner

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay that Agni indeed sit down (at our sacrifice), who in every age of man has been the invoker of the gods, doer of wise deeds, the messenger of the gods, the bearer of oblations.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

For he is the one who has sat through the human (life)spans as Hotar with a poetтАЩs purpose,
and as the messenger conveying the oblations.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The injunc. s─л╠Бdat, in conjunction with the acc. of extent of time m─Б╠Бnuс╣г─Б yug─Б╠БтАЬthrough the human lifetimes,тАЭ seems almost to have shed the literal sense of the root тИЪsad тАШsitтАЩ in favor of expressing pure durativity (тАЬwho, through the human lifetimes, has (always) been тАжтАЭ) – though the immediately following h├│t─Б evokes the standard phrase for the installation of Agni as Hotar, with the full тАШsitтАЩ clearly present if metaphorically meant. as in VI.1.2 ├бdh─Б h├│t─Б ny ├аs─лdaс╕е тАж (тАЬthen you sat down as HotarтАЭ) in this Agni cycle. I rather imagine both senses are meant.

+Griffith

For as sagacious Herald he hath sat through every age of man,
Oblation-bearing messenger.

+Geldner

Denn er ist es, der die menschlichen Zeitalter hindurch als Hotri mit Sehersinn dasitzt und der opferfahrende Bote ist.

+Grassmann

Denn alle Menschenalter durch sass er als weiser Priester da, Als Bote, der die Opfer f├дhrt.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬSon of strength, Agni, the glorious radiance of you who are immortal, bestows food upon (your) mortal worshipper.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Good is your manifestation, Agni, for the prospering mortalтАФ
(the manifestation) of (you) the immortal, o child of nourishment.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Given the proximity of ┼л╠Бrj- тАШ(solid) nourishmentтАЩ beginning c, iс╣гayat├й in b might better be rendered in a manner closer to ├нс╣г- тАШrefreshmentтАЩ in the same semantic domain. So Geldner тАЬf├╝r die speisew├╝nschenden Sterblichen,тАЭ Renou тАЬpour le mortel cherchant la jouissance.тАЭ I might suggest an alternative тАЬтАж for the mortal seeking refreshment, / o child of nourishment.тАЭ What gives me pause, however, is iс╣г├бyantaс╕е in vs. 27 in the same tс╣Ыca, where the тАШprosperтАЩ sense is favored. Although our dat. part. has accent on the ending, whereas iс╣г├бyantaс╕е has (secondary) тАЬcausativeтАЭ accent, in fact oblique forms of -├бya-participles seem regularly to have desinential accent: cf. mahayat├й (VII.32.9) to mah├бyati, kс╣Ыpayat├бс╕е (VIII.46.16) to kс╣Ыp├бyati. See disc. in my 1983 -├бya-book, p. 49 with n. 3. Therefore these two nearby forms are likely to belong to the same stem and invite the same tr.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay the donor (of the oblation), propitiating you by his acts today, be exalted, and (rendered) very opulent; may (such) mortal be diligent in (your) praise.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Acccording to your will let the giver be best off, winning you today, acquiring a good legacy.
The mortal has achieved a (hymn) with a good twist.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The kr├бtu- is presumably AgniтАЩs; cf. vs. 23 kav├нkratuс╕е used of him. Geldner tr.

kr├бtv─Б as тАЬMit dem Gedanken,тАЭ and takes the interior p─Бdas bc as the directly quoted content of that thought. In addition to the aberrant tr. of kr├бtu- (though one could tr.

тАЬwith the intentionтАЭ), this seems unnecessary. Although, as Geldner notes, kr├бtv─Б in IV.1.1 does introduce such direct speech, it is marked there by ├нti, and the circumstances there are different as well.

+Griffith

Rich through his wisdom, noblest be the giver serving thee to-day:
The man hath brought his hymn of praise.

+Geldner

Mit dem Gedanken: “Der Geber soll der Vorz├╝glichste sein, der Reiche, der dich heute, o Agni, gewinnt hat der Sterbliche den Lobpreis auf dich zuwege gebracht.

+Grassmann

Heilsamst sei der reiche Geber, der dich willig heut beschenket, Loblied hat der Mann ersonnen.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the close sandhi effect in the voc. phrase brahmaс╣Зas kave. As Geldner points out, this p─Бda is a variant of I.18.3 r├бkс╣г─Б с╣Зo brahmaс╣Зas pate, with the more usual head noun p├бti-. Because it is part of a voc. phrase and such phrases show close sandhi effects elsewhere, this does not necessarily belong with the other instances of irregular sandhi of -s before kav├н-, on which see comm. ad VII.18.2, though that may be a factor.

+Wilson

+Jamison Brereton

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I do not know what the ─Б╠Бending the first p─Бda is doing. S─Бyaс╣Зa. takes it as preverb with d─Б╠Б┼Ыati, but this root doesnтАЩt otherwise appear with ─Б╠Б, and p─Бda-final position is a strange place to put a preverb. ThereтАЩs a p─Бda-final ─Б╠Бalso in 35a, but it is easier to justify, as governing a locational acc. I am disturbed by the usage of d─Б╠Б┼Ыati here; for another problematic form to this root, see disc. ad vs. 20 above. The example here describes not pious service but a hostile act exactly contrary to the standard usages of the root. It also deviates from the usual case frame (offer service to a god [DAT] with an offering vel sim. [INSTR]), though a few passages match ours by expressing the offering in the ACC, e.g. I.93.3 тАж y├б ─Б╠Бhutiс╣Г, y├│ v─Бс╣Г d─Б╠Б┼Ы─Бd dhav├нс╣гkс╣Ыtim тАЬwhoever will piously perform a poured offering or the preparation of an oblation for you.тАЭ Assuming the reading is correct, I think we must see this as a monstrous reversal: instead of piously offering an oblation (ACC) to a god (DAT), the evil mortal is impiously offering us (ACC), as a sort of oblation, to a weapon of death (DAT). The standard tr. (including mine) elide the shock of the use of this verb of ritual service in such a context, by tr. тИЪd─Б┼Ы differently from usual. But IтАЩm not sure how to remedy this in tr. without a lot of explanatory baggage. Perhaps тАЬwho will тАШpiouslyтАЩ offer us тАжтАЭ? Geldner and Renou take t├бsm─Бt тАж ├бс╣Гhasaс╕е as a single NP тАЬfrom that ├бс╣Гhas-,тАЭ but this requires taking y├бс╕е in p─Бda a as an improper rel. for тАЬwhenтАЭ (so Geldner) or seeing the relation between ab and c as an anacoluthon (so Renou), because their interpr. of c provides no referent for y├бс╕е тАж m├бrtaс╕е in the dependent cl. This can all be fixed by separating the two abl. in the main clause, with t├бsm─Бt the correlative to y├бс╕е. Since the immediately preceding vs. (30) has exactly the structure envisioned for our c p─Бda – two parallel ablatives, one ├бс╣Гhasaс╕е and the other referring to a person – there is very local precedent.

+Griffith

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬRadiant in the embryo of the maternal (earth), on the imperishable (altar); the cherisher of the paternal (heaven), sitting on the seat of sacrifice.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The cherisher: he m─Бtuс╕е, putuс╣гpit─Б: the mother of Agni is the earth, the father is heaven; Agni is said to be the father or fosterer of his parent heaven, by transmitting to it the flame and smoke of burnt-offerings

+Jamison Brereton

In the womb of his mother, as the father of his father, having flashed forth at the imperishable (syllable?),
sitting on the birthplace of truthтАФ

+Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. is syntactically incomplete (unless we take s─л╠Бdan in c as a predicated pres. part., which seems unlikely, since this is a repeated p─Бda [=IX.32.4, IX.64.11]), but it works well as adjunct to the previous vs., 34.

P─Бda a shows the preoccupation with kinship that is characteristic of Agni material. The paradox тАЬfather of his fatherтАЭ (pit├║с╣г pit─Б╠Б[note close sandhi effect]) probably reflects two themes – 1) that the priest who kindles the fire is in some sense his/its father, but Agni the god has a fatherly relationship to his mortal worshipers, 2) that the offering fire (later called the ─Аhavan─лya) is тАЬtaken outтАЭ of what is later called the G─Бrhapatya and is therefore in some sense its son, but the offering fire is more important than the other fires on the ritual ground and can therefore be considered their father.

The meaning тАШsyllableтАЩ for akс╣г├бra- is quite stable in later Skt., but in the RV it sometimes has its literal sense тАШimperishableтАЩ. Nonetheless in our passage I think тАШsyllableтАЩ is meant: the ritual fire is kindled when the hymn (here represented by the syllable) is recited. So, more or less, Geldner тАЬbei der (heiligen) Rede (?) aufleuchtendтАЭ (sim. K├╝mmel 250), though cf. Renou тАЬdans (l’espace) in├йpuissable.тАЭ The p─Бda-final ─Б╠Бin c was mentioned above ad vs. 31, where it was pointed out that the occurrence here in 35c can easily be accounted for. ─Б╠Бfrequently governs a preceding acc. (see collection in Grassmann, col. 169), and in fact y├│nim ─Б╠Бis found not only in this p─Бda and its repetitions (see above), but also in similar p─Бdas in IX.61.21, 65.19).

+Griffith

His Father’s Father, shining in his Mother’s everlasting side,
Set on the seat of holy Law.

+Geldner

Im Leibe der Mutter Vater seines Vaters, bei der heiligen Rede aufleuchtend, sich in den Scho├Я der Opferordnung setzend,

+Grassmann

Des Vaters Vater, strahlend hell im Mutterleib, im Aetherraum Sich setzend in des Opfers Schooss.

+Elizarenkova

(sunтАЩs) heat,
o Agni of golden appearanceтАФ794 VI.17

Agni, who glitterest like gold.

+Elizarenkova

Agni is identified with Rudra as the destoyer of the cities of Tripura: rudro v─Б eс╣гo yad agniс╕е

+Jamison Brereton

You who, like a powerful sharpshooter, like a sharp-horned buffalo, have broken strongholds, o Agni.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Unlike most -h├бn- cmpds, whose 1st member is the target of the smiting, in ┼Ыarya-h├бn- the 1st member ┼Ыarya- тАШarrowтАЩ must be in an instr. relationship with the 2nd (see Scarlatta 693), like muс╣гс╣нi-h├бn тАШsmiting with the fist(s)тАЩ. Because тАЬlike a powerful shooter with arrows / one who shoots arrowsтАЭ is exceptionally awk in English, IтАЩve substituted тАШsharpshooterтАЩ, though it interferes with the tigm├б- in tigm├б-┼Ыс╣Ыс╣Еga- тАШsharp-hornedтАЩ in the next p─Бda.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The simile marker n├б is wrongly placed in p─Бda b, for no obvious reason.

The two comparanda to Agni – a bangle in the hand, a newborn babe, both carried – suggest that this is the newly kindled fire, probably the offering fire, being taken out of the householderтАЩs fire and carried to the east.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬ(Welcome him) as soon as born, like a beloved guest, and plural ce the lord of the mansion upon the sacred (altar) whence wisdom is derived.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

This and previous с╣Ыca are recited when the fire that has been produced by attrition is applied to kindle the ─Бhavan─лya, or fire of burnt-offerings; Aitareya Br─Бhman.a 1.16; Agni is the guest, not the sacriicer, of the ─Бhavan─лya fire; j─Бtavedasi is applied to the latter, as knowing the birth of the churned fire, to whom it is a giver of delight, ┼Ыyona, sukhakara, by giving him a welcome reception.

+Jamison Brereton

тАЬWhetтАЭ the dear guest, just born on (the old fire) J─Бtavedas,
the houselord in his comfortable (birth)place.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

However, the waters are somewhat muddied by vs. 42. The loc. j─Бt├бvedasi (the only such form in the RV) is puzzling, since j─Бt├бvedas- is one of the standard epithets of Agni and the accusatives in the vs. clearly refer to Agni as well. Thus we must be dealing with two fires. This idea would be perfectly compatible with the scenario I suggested for vs. 40 – except that acc. gс╣Ыhap├бtim in p─Бda c suggests that the newly born fire being тАЬwhettedтАЭ is not the offering fire (later to be called the ─Аhavan─лya) taken out of the old fire and moved to its new location, but rather what will come to be called the G─Бrhapatya. The (later) ritual complex that our passage most resembles is the creation of the Mah─Бvedi (see my Hyenas, p. 89, inter alia), in which the old ─Аhavan─лya of the standard ritual ground is moved further to the east during the creation of the Mah─Бvedi, and the old ─Аhavan─лya becomes the G─Бrhapatya.

Thus it seems that vss. 40-41 concern the further displacement of the ─Аhavan─лya fire and 42 depicts the resettlement of the original householderтАЩs fire onto the place the ─Аhavan─лya occupied in the more restricted ritual ground. This may be GeldnerтАЩs view; see his n. 41ab, where he refers to the agnipraс╣Зayana, which is the technical term for carrying the ─Аhavan─лya to the Uttaravedi in the animal sacrifice (see Sen, Dict. of Vedic Rituals, s.v.; Caland-Henry, Agniс╣гс╣нoma pp. 78-79). However, his n. 42 goes in a different direction. If this really does concern the creation of the Mah─Бvedi from the ordinary ritual ground, we would have evidence for this degree of elaboration already in (late) Rigvedic ritual.

+Geldner

+Grassmann

+Elizarenkova

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The h├н in the impv. clause is somewhat disturbing, since there is no following impv. in this vs. to which the h├н impv. clause could serve as basis.

However, 44a contains two impvs. that logically follow the yukс╣гv─Б╠БтАШyoke!тАЩ – namely y─Бhi ─Б╠Бvaha тАЬdrive and convey here!тАЭ and so the usual use of h├н in impv. clauses can be seen here, across two vss.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhatever mortal, offering oblations, worships a deity with (sacrificial) food, let him at the ceremony also worship Agni, the invoker of heaven and earth, the sacrificer with truth; let him adore (Agni) with uplifted hands.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The mortal who with pursuit would seek friendship with the god, he, offering oblations at the ceremony, should reverently invoke Agni.
With outstretched hands he should seek to win with homage the Hotar whose sacrifice comes true in the two world-halves.

+Griffith

The mortal man who serves the God with banquet, and, bringing gifts at sacrifice, lauds Agni,
May well attract, with prayer and hands uplifted, the Priest of Heaven and Earth, true Sacrificer.

+Geldner

Welcher Sterbliche dem Gott durch Einladung die schuldige Ehre erweisen m├╢chte, der soll Agni mit Spenden zum Gottesdienst berufen. Er soll den wahrhaft opfernden Hotri beider Welten mit ausgestreckten H├дnden unter Verneigung herbitten.

+Grassmann

Der Sterbliche, welcher den Gott mit Opferspeise beschenkt, und den Agni beim Feste preist mit Trank versehen, der mag den wahren Opfrer beider Welten die Hand austreckend durch Gebet gewinnen.

+Elizarenkova

рдЕрдирдпрд╛рдзреНрдпрдпрдирдВ рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрдпрдд рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рд╢реНрд╡рд▓рд╛рдпрдиреЛ рдордиреНрдпрддреЗ (рдЖрд╢реНрд╡. рдЧреГ. рез. рез. рел)ред рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рддреЗ рддреБрднреНрдпрдВ рд╣реГрджрд╛ рд╣реГрджрдпреЗрди рддрд╖реНрдЯрдВ рд╕рдВрд╕реНрдХреГрддрдореН рдЛрдЪрд╛ рдЛрдЧреНрд░реВрдкреЗрдг рд╡рд░реНрддрдорд╛рдирдВ рд╣рд╡рд┐рдГ рдЛрдЪрдореЗрд╡ рд╣рд╡рд┐рдГ рдХреГрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдЖ рднрд░рд╛рдорд╕рд┐ рдЖрд╣рд░рд╛рдордГ ред рдд рдЗрддрд┐ рддрдЪреНрдЫрдмреНрджреЗрди рдкреНрд░рдХреГрддрдореГрдЧреНрд░реВрдкрдВ рд╣рд╡рд┐рдГ рдкрд░рд╛рдореГрд╢реНрдпрддреЗ ред рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдирд┐рд░реНрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдкреЗрдХреНрд╖рдпрд╛ рдкреБрдВрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдмрд╣реБрддреНрд╡реЗ ред рдЛрдЧреНрд░реВрдкрдВ рддрджреНрдзрд╡рд┐рдГ рддреЗ рддреБрднреНрдпрдореН рдЙрдХреНрд╖рдгрдГ рдЙрдХреНрд╖рд╛рдгрдГ рд╕реЗрдЪрдирд╕рдорд░реНрдерд╛рдГ рдЛрд╖рднрд╛рд╕рдГ рдЛрд╖рднрд╛рдГ рдЙрдд рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рд╡рд╢рд╛рдГ рдЪ рднрд╡рдиреНрддреБ ред рдЛрд╖рднрд╡рд╢рд╛рд░реВрдкреЗрдг рдкрд░рд┐рдгрддрдВ рд╕рддреН рддреНрд╡рджреНрднрдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рдп рднрд╡рддреНрд╡рд┐рддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ рее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWe offer to you, Agni, the oblation sanctified by the heart, and (identified) with the sacred verse may the vigorous bulls and the cows be (as such an oblation) to you.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

May the vigorous bulls and the cows: te te bhavantu ┼лkс╣гaс╣Зa rс╣гabh─Бso va┼Ы─Б uta, may these vigorous bulls or the cows be for you; an intimation of their being offered to Agni as victims rс╣гabhavaс╣г─Бr┼лpeс╣Зa pariс╣Зatam san tvabhakс╣гa с╣З─Бya (havir) bhavatu, let the oblation, matured in the form of bulls or cows, be for your food

+Jamison Brereton

Here to you, Agni, we bring with a verse an oblation fashioned by our heart:
let the oxen, bulls, and mated cows be yours.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Bloomfield (ad V.6.5) proposes tr. our passage тАЬWe bring … oblation with song fashioned in the mind,тАЭ suggesting that тАЬthe cases of с╣Ыc─Б╠Бand hav├нс╕е are inverted.тАЭ This is certainly true at the level of deep-structure formula: hс╣Ыd─Б╠Бtaс╣гс╣н├б- тАЬfashioned by the heartтАЭ normally modifies a verbal product, e.g. I.171.2 st├│mo hс╣Ыd─Б╠Бtaс╣гс╣н├бс╕е. But, as so often, the poet is playing with our expections by producing a twist on the standard phraseology.

+Griffith

Agni, we bring thee, with our hymn, oblation fashioned in the heart.
Let these be oxen unto thee, let these be bulls and kine to thee.

+Geldner

Wir bringen dir, o Agni, mit einem Vers ein Opfer, das mit dem Herzen gedichtet ist, denn das sollen deine Ochsen, Stiere und K├╝he sein.

+Grassmann

Wir bringen dir, o Agni, unter Gesang den aus liebendem Herzen bereiteten Trank dar; dein seien auch diese Ochsen, Stiere und K├╝he.

+Elizarenkova
